style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Sources: UK <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a> at <a href="/wiki/National_Air_Traffic_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="National Air Traffic Services">NATS</a><sup id="cite_ref-aip_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><br />Statistics from the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">UK Civil Aviation Authority</a><sup id="cite_ref-auto2_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><br />Location from Glasgow Airport<sup id="cite_ref-location_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-location-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Glasgow Airport</b>, also known as <b>Glasgow International Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>GLA<sup id="cite_ref-IATA_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IATA-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EGPF</b>), formerly <i>Abbotsinch Airport</i>, is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>. It is located in <a href="/wiki/Paisley,_Renfrewshire" title="Paisley, Renfrewshire">Paisley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renfrewshire" title="Renfrewshire">Renfrewshire</a>, 8.6 <a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">nautical miles</a> (15.9&#160;km; 9.9&#160;mi) west<sup id="cite_ref-aip_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> of <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> city centre. In 2019, the airport handled 8.84&#160;million passengers, an 8.4% annual decrease, making it the second-busiest in Scotland, after <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport" title="Edinburgh Airport">Edinburgh Airport</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Busiest_airports_in_the_United_Kingdom_by_total_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Busiest airports in the United Kingdom by total passenger traffic">ninth-busiest airport in the United Kingdom</a>.\n</p><p>The airport is owned and operated by <a href="/wiki/AGS_Airports" title="AGS Airports">AGS Airports</a> which also owns and operates <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_Airport" title="Aberdeen Airport">Aberdeen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Airport" title="Southampton Airport">Southampton Airports</a>. It was previously owned and operated by <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport_Holdings" title="Heathrow Airport Holdings">Heathrow Airport Holdings</a> (formerly known as BAA).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The airport\'s largest tenants are <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Loganair" title="Loganair">Loganair</a>, the latter using it as a <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Other major airlines using Glasgow as a base include <a href="/wiki/Jet2.com" title="Jet2.com">Jet2</a> and <a href="/wiki/TUI_Airways" title="TUI Airways">TUI Airways</a> (formerly known as Thomson Airways).\n</p><p>Glasgow Airport was opened in 1966 and originally flights only operated to other places in the United Kingdom and Europe. Glasgow Airport began to offer flights to other places around the world, flights which previously used <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Prestwick_Airport" title="Glasgow Prestwick Airport">Glasgow Prestwick Airport</a>, which was subsequently relegated as the city\'s secondary airport catering for <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost airlines</a>, freight and charter operators.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#1940"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">1940</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#1960s"><span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Plans"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Plans</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Proposed_rail_link"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Proposed rail link</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The history of the present Glasgow Airport goes back to 1932, when the site at <a href="/wiki/Abbotsinch" title="Abbotsinch">Abbotsinch</a>, between the <a href="/wiki/River_Cart#Black_Cart_Water" title="River Cart">Black Cart Water</a> and the <a href="/wiki/River_Cart#White_Cart_Water" title="River Cart">White Cart Water</a>, near Paisley in Renfrewshire, was opened. In 1933 the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> <a href="/wiki/No._602_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 602 Squadron RAF">602 Squadron</a> (City of Glasgow) <a href="/wiki/Royal_Auxiliary_Air_Force" title="Royal Auxiliary Air Force">Auxiliary Air Force</a> moved its <a href="/wiki/Westland_Wapiti" title="Westland Wapiti">Wapiti IIA</a> aircraft from nearby Renfrew.<sup id="cite_ref-smith-abbotsinch_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith-abbotsinch-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The RAF Station HQ, however, was not formed until 1 July 1936 when 6 Auxiliary Group, <a href="/wiki/RAF_Bomber_Command" title="RAF Bomber Command">Bomber Command</a>, arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-smith-abbotsinch_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith-abbotsinch-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> From May 1939, until moving away in October 1939, the Squadron flew the <a href="/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">Supermarine Spitfire</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1940">1940</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1940">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1940, a <a href="/wiki/Torpedo" title="Torpedo">torpedo</a> training unit was formed, which trained both RAF and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> crews.<sup id="cite_ref-smith-abbotsinch_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith-abbotsinch-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> On 11 August 1943 Abbotsinch was handed over solely to the Royal Navy and it became a <a href="/wiki/Stone_frigate" title="Stone frigate">naval base</a>. All <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Ship" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Ship">Her Majesty\'s Ships</a> and naval bases are given ship names and Abbotsinch\'s was known as HMS Sanderling since June 1940.<sup id="cite_ref-smith-abbotsinch_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith-abbotsinch-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> During the 1950s, the airfield housed a large aircraft storage unit and squadrons of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Reserve" title="Royal Naval Reserve">Royal Naval Volunteer Reserve</a>.\n</p><p>The Royal Navy left in October 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-smith-abbotsinch_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith-abbotsinch-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The name <a href="/wiki/Sanderling" title="Sanderling">Sanderling</a> was, however, retained as a link between the two: HMS Sanderling\'s <a href="/wiki/Ship%27s_bell" title="Ship&#39;s bell">ship\'s bell</a> was presented to the new airport and a bar in the airport was named <i>The Sanderling Bar</i>.\n</p><p>The following units were here at some point:<sup id="cite_ref-ABCT_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABCT-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output Glasgow and Strathclyde Air Squadron</a></li></ul></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960s">1960s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1960s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the 1960s, <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Glasgow" title="Politics of Glasgow">Glasgow Corporation</a> decided that a new airport for the city was required. The original site of Glasgow\'s main airport, <a href="/wiki/Renfrew_Airport" title="Renfrew Airport">Renfrew Airport</a>, was 3&#160;km (1.9&#160;mi) east of Abbotsinch, in what is now the Dean Park area of Renfrew. The original <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> terminal building of the original airport has not survived. The site is now occupied by a <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a> supermarket and the <a href="/wiki/M8_motorway_(Scotland)" title="M8 motorway (Scotland)">M8 motorway</a>; this straight and level section of motorway occupies the site of the <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-smith-renfrew_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith-renfrew-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Abbotsinch took over from Renfrew Airport on 2 May 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-smith-abbotsinch_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith-abbotsinch-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smith-renfrew_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith-renfrew-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Government">UK Government</a> had already committed millions into rebuilding <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Prestwick_Airport" title="Glasgow Prestwick Airport">Prestwick Airport</a> fit for the "<a href="/wiki/Jet_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Jet age">jet age</a>". Nevertheless, the plan went forward and the new airport, designed by <a href="/wiki/Basil_Spence" title="Basil Spence">Basil Spence</a> and built at a cost of \xc2\xa34.2&#160;million, was completed in 1966, with <a href="/wiki/British_European_Airways" title="British European Airways">British European Airways</a> beginning services using <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Comet" title="De Havilland Comet">De Havilland Comet</a> aircraft.\n</p><p>The first commercial flight to arrive was a British European Airways flight from Edinburgh, landing at 8&#160;am on 2 May 1966.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The airport was officially opened on 27 June 1966 by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>. The political rows over Glasgow and Prestwick airports continued, with Prestwick enjoying a monopoly over <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_flight" title="Transatlantic flight">transatlantic</a> traffic (under the 1946 US-UK <a href="/wiki/Bilateral_air_transport_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilateral air transport agreement">bilateral air transport agreement</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Agreement" title="Bermuda Agreement">Bermuda Agreement</a>), while Glasgow Airport was only allowed to handle UK and intra-European traffic.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s_to_1990s">1970s to 1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1970s to 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Aftermath_-_geograph.org.uk_-_485211.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Aftermath_-_geograph.org.uk_-_485211.jpg/220px-The_Aftermath_-_geograph.org.uk_-_485211.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Aftermath_-_geograph.org.uk_-_485211.jpg/330px-The_Aftermath_-_geograph.org.uk_-_485211.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Aftermath_-_geograph.org.uk_-_485211.jpg/440px-The_Aftermath_-_geograph.org.uk_-_485211.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Aftermath_-_geograph.org.uk_-_485211.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/2007_Glasgow_International_Airport_attack" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Glasgow International Airport attack">2007 Glasgow International Airport attack</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1975, the BAA took ownership of Glasgow Airport. When BAA was <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatised</a> in the late 1980s, as BAA plc, it consolidated its airport portfolio and sold Prestwick Airport. BAA embarked on a massive redevelopment plan for Glasgow International Airport in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An extended terminal building was created by building a pre-fabricated metal structure around the front of the original Basil Spence building, hence screening much of its distinctive <a href="/wiki/Brutalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Brutalism">Brutalist</a> style architecture from view, with the void between the two structures joined by a glass atrium and walkway. Spence\'s original concrete facade which once looked onto Caledonia Road now fronts the <a href="/wiki/Check-in" title="Check-in">check-in</a> desks. The original building can be seen more clearly from the rear, with the mock barrel-vaulted roof visible when airside.\n</p><p>A dedicated international departure lounge and pier was added at the western side of the building, leaving the facility with a total of 38 <a href="/wiki/Gate_(airport)" title="Gate (airport)">gates</a>, bringing its capacity up to nine million passengers per year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 2003, BAA completed redevelopment work on a satellite building (called "T2", formerly the St. Andrews Building), to provide a dedicated check-in facility for low-cost airlines, principally Aer Lingus, Virgin Atlantic Airways and formerly <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Airlines" title="Thomas Cook Airlines">Thomas Cook Airlines</a> until they went into administration.\n</p><p>By 1996, Glasgow was handling over 5.5&#160;million passengers per annum, making it the fourth-largest airport in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_2000">Post 2000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Post 2000">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:217px;"><a href="/wiki/File:16-11-16-Glasgow_Airport-RR2_7310.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/16-11-16-Glasgow_Airport-RR2_7310.jpg/215px-16-11-16-Glasgow_Airport-RR2_7310.jpg" decoding="async" width="215" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/16-11-16-Glasgow_Airport-RR2_7310.jpg/323px-16-11-16-Glasgow_Airport-RR2_7310.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/16-11-16-Glasgow_Airport-RR2_7310.jpg/430px-16-11-16-Glasgow_Airport-RR2_7310.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:16-11-16-Glasgow_Airport-RR2_7310.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 2 building, situated next to the main terminal building</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgowairport3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Glasgowairport3.jpg/220px-Glasgowairport3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="52" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Glasgowairport3.jpg/330px-Glasgowairport3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Glasgowairport3.jpg/440px-Glasgowairport3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2660" data-file-height="623" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgowairport3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tail fins at the international pier</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:217px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow_Airport_DSC_0856_(13765675113).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Glasgow_Airport_DSC_0856_%2813765675113%29.jpg/215px-Glasgow_Airport_DSC_0856_%2813765675113%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="215" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Glasgow_Airport_DSC_0856_%2813765675113%29.jpg/323px-Glasgow_Airport_DSC_0856_%2813765675113%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Glasgow_Airport_DSC_0856_%2813765675113%29.jpg/430px-Glasgow_Airport_DSC_0856_%2813765675113%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow_Airport_DSC_0856_(13765675113).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Glasgow Airport main terminal building</div></div></div>\n<p>The airport serves a variety of destinations throughout Europe, North America and the Middle East. <a href="/wiki/Jet2.com" title="Jet2.com">Jet2</a>, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a>, <a href="/wiki/TUI_Airways" title="TUI Airways">TUI Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Loganair" title="Loganair">Loganair</a> have a base at the airport.\n</p><p>The terminal consists of three piers; the West Pier, Central Pier and East Pier.\n</p><p>The West Pier, commonly known as the International Pier, was built as part of the 1989 extension project and is the principal international and long haul departure point. All but two of the stands on this pier are equipped with airbridges. This pier has stands 27 - 36.<sup id="cite_ref-eurocontrol.int_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurocontrol.int-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> From 2019, the pier will have the ability to facilitate the A380 following an \xc2\xa38 million upgrade.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Central Pier was part of the original 1966 building. The British Airways gates are located in the 1971 extension at the end of the pier, with <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow">Heathrow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick</a> shuttles making up most of its traffic as well as <a href="/wiki/BA_CityFlyer" title="BA CityFlyer">BA CityFlyer</a> flights to <a href="/wiki/London_City_Airport" title="London City Airport">London City</a>. The British Airways lounge is located on this pier, across from gate 15. Other users of the Central Pier are <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a> and formerly <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a>. Most of the stands on this pier are equipped with airbridges. This pier has stands 14 - 26.<sup id="cite_ref-eurocontrol.int_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurocontrol.int-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The East Pier, constructed in the mid-1970s, was originally used for international flights but in recent years has been re-developed for use by low-cost airlines. None of the stands on this pier are equipped with airbridges. The main users of this pier are Ryanair, easyJet, Jet2 and Loganair. In 2015 a \xc2\xa33,000,000 extension was added to the pier, creating space for 750,000 extra passengers a year. This pier has stands 1- 12.<sup id="cite_ref-eurocontrol.int_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurocontrol.int-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In late 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> work commenced on Skyhub (located between the Main Terminal and Terminal 2)<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> which created a single, purpose-built security screening area in place of the previous individual facilities for each of the three piers, the other side effect being an enlarged duty-free shopping area created by taking most of the previous landside shopping and restaurant facilities airside. This new arrangement also frees up space in the departure lounges through the removal of the separate duty-free shops in the West and Central Piers. This however meant that the former public viewing areas of the apron are now airside, making the airport inaccessible to aviation enthusiasts and spectators.\n</p><p>Future growth is hampered by the airport\'s location, which is constrained by the M8 motorway to the south, the town of Renfrew to the east and the <a href="/wiki/River_Clyde" title="River Clyde">River Clyde</a> to the north. At present the areas of <a href="/wiki/Drumchapel" title="Drumchapel">Drumchapel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clydebank" title="Clydebank">Clydebank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bearsden" title="Bearsden">Bearsden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foxbar" title="Foxbar">Foxbar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faifley" title="Faifley">Faifley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linwood,_Renfrewshire" title="Linwood, Renfrewshire">Linwood</a> all sit directly underneath the approach paths into the airport, meaning that further increases in traffic may be politically sensitive. The airport is challenged by <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport" title="Edinburgh Airport">Edinburgh Airport</a>, which now serves a wider range of European destinations and has grown to overtake Glasgow as Scotland\'s busiest airport.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Executive</a> announced in 2002 that a rail line \xe2\x80\x93 known as the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport_Rail_Link" title="Glasgow Airport Rail Link">Glasgow Airport Rail Link</a> (GARL) \xe2\x80\x93 would be built from <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_station" title="Glasgow Central station">Glasgow Central station</a> to Glasgow Airport. The rail link was to be completed by 2012 with the first trains running early in 2013. In 2009, however, it was announced by the Scottish Government that the plan had been cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Currently, the airport is easily accessible by road due with direct access to the adjoining M8 motorway. It is also served by a frequent bus service, the Glasgow Airport Express, which operates services to <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_city_centre" title="Glasgow city centre">city centre</a>. The service is run by <a href="/wiki/First_Glasgow" title="First Glasgow">First Glasgow</a> and all buses feature leather seats, USB charging ports and free WiFi.\n</p><p>The airport is home to the Scottish <a href="/wiki/Regional_airline" title="Regional airline">regional airline</a> Loganair, previously a Flybe franchise operator, who have their head office located on site.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> British Airways has a maintenance <a href="/wiki/Hangar" title="Hangar">hangar</a> at the airport, capable of carrying out overhaul work on <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320</a>, as well as a cargo facility.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> also has a unit based within the airport \xe2\x80\x93 The <a href="/wiki/Universities_of_Glasgow_and_Strathclyde_Air_Squadron" title="Universities of Glasgow and Strathclyde Air Squadron">Universities of Glasgow and Strathclyde Air Squadron</a> \xe2\x80\x93 to provide flying training to university students who plan to join the RAF.\n</p><p>In 2007, Glasgow became the second-busiest airport in Scotland as passenger numbers were surpassed by those at <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport" title="Edinburgh Airport">Edinburgh Airport</a>.\n</p><p>Icelandair temporarily moved its base of operations from <a href="/wiki/Keflav%C3%ADk_International_Airport" title="Keflav\xc3\xadk International Airport">Keflav\xc3\xadk International Airport</a> to Glasgow due to the <a href="/wiki/2010_eruptions_of_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="2010 eruptions of Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull">2010 eruptions of Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull</a>.\n</p><p>On 10 April 2014, <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> operated an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> to Glasgow to celebrate the 10th anniversary of the Glasgow - Dubai route, the first time an A380 had visited a Scottish airport.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2014, Emirates opened a dedicated lounge at the airport<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> for First and Business class passengers. It is located at the top of the West Pier. In October 2014, Heathrow Airport Holdings reached an agreement to sell the airport, together with Southampton and Aberdeen, to a consortium of Ferrovial and <a href="/wiki/Macquarie_Group" title="Macquarie Group">Macquarie Group</a> for \xc2\xa31&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017 <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> became the first airline to carry more than one million passengers from the airport in a period of 12 months.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 February 2018, <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> announced that it would close its base at Glasgow, and retain just three of its 22 routes. It cited the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a>\'s failure to replace <a href="/wiki/Air_Passenger_Duty" title="Air Passenger Duty">Air Passenger Duty</a> with a cheaper <a href="/wiki/Air_Departure_Tax" title="Air Departure Tax">Air Departure Tax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 16 April 2019, Emirates launched a daily A380 flight on the Glasgow - Dubai route, making it the first regular A380 service in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plans">Plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 2005, BAA published a consultation paper<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> for the development of the airport. The consultation paper included proposals for a second runway parallel to and to the north-west of the existing runway 05/23; redevelopment and enlargement of the East (low-cost) pier to connect directly with Terminal 2; and an additional International Pier to the west of the existing International Pier. There were plans for a new rail terminal, joined to the airport\'s passenger terminal and <a href="/wiki/Multi-storey_car_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-storey car park">multi-storey car park</a>. On 29 November 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> gave the go-ahead for the new railway station as part of the Glasgow Airport Rail Link to Glasgow Central station, originally due for completion in 2011. However, on 17 September 2009, due to escalating costs, the project was cancelled by the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BAA\'s plans, which are expected to cost some \xc2\xa3290&#160;million over the next 25 years, come in response to a forecasted trebling of annual passenger numbers passing through the airport by 2030. The current figure of 9.4&#160;million passengers passing through the airport is expected to rise to more than 24 million by 2030.\n</p><p>As of late 2017, there are plans to build a light rail link that will connect the city centre to the airport via <a href="/wiki/Govan" title="Govan">Govan</a>, with plans already underway to begin construction of the project after the cancellation of the original <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport_Rail_Link" title="Glasgow Airport Rail Link">Glasgow Airport Rail Link</a> project.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled and charter services to and from Glasgow:<sup id="cite_ref-glasgowairport.com_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-glasgowairport.com-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> 2.6%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>On 3 September 1999, a <a href="/wiki/Cessna_404" class="mw-redirect" title="Cessna 404">Cessna 404</a> carrying nine <a href="/wiki/MyTravel_Group" title="MyTravel Group">Airtours</a> staff from Glasgow to <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a> on a transfer flight, <a href="/wiki/1999_Glasgow_Airport_Cessna_404_crash" title="1999 Glasgow Airport Cessna 404 crash">crashed</a> minutes after takeoff near the town of Linwood, Renfrewshire. Eight people were killed and three seriously injured. No one on the ground was hurt.<sup id="cite_ref-FAI_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAI-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Air_Accident_Investigation_Branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Accident Investigation Branch">Air Accident Investigation Branch</a> report on the accident later found that the aircraft developed an engine malfunction during takeoff. Although the captain decided to return to the airfield, he mistakenly identified the working engine as the faulty one and shut it down, causing the aircraft to crash.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Fatal_accident_inquiry" title="Fatal accident inquiry">fatal accident inquiry</a> was also held,<sup id="cite_ref-FAI_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAI-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> which reached the same conclusion.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 30 June 2007, a day after the <a href="/wiki/2007_London_car_bombs" title="2007 London car bombs">failed car bomb attacks in London</a>, an <a href="/wiki/2007_Glasgow_Airport_attack" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Glasgow Airport attack">attack at Glasgow International Airport</a> occurred. A flaming <a href="/wiki/Jeep_Cherokee_(XJ)" title="Jeep Cherokee (XJ)">Jeep Cherokee</a> was driven into the entrance of Main Terminal. Two men, one alight, fled the vehicle before being apprehended by a combination of police officers, airport security officers and witnesses. One of the men died in the following months due to injuries sustained in the attack. New barriers and security measures have been added to prevent a similar incident from taking place.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On October 4, 2019 a <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> flight recently arrived from <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> and the airport\'s international section were evacuated after <a href="/wiki/Dry_ice" title="Dry ice">dry ice</a> around a shipment of <a href="/wiki/Vaccine" title="Vaccine">vaccines</a> leaked in the aircraft\'s hold. Emergency services later declared the cargo safe.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On November 8, 2020 a Czech man was arrested after checking in three suitcases containing <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">\xc2\xa3</a>867,520 for a flight to <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>. He had arrived at <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Edinburgh International Airport">Edinburgh</a> from <a href="/wiki/Prague_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Prague International Airport">Prague</a> the day before carrying only a small holdall, before collecting the cash at Glasgow\'s <a href="/wiki/Marriott_Hotel" class="mw-redirect" title="Marriott Hotel">Marriott Hotel</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Crown_Office_and_Procurator_Fiscal_Service" title="Crown Office and Procurator Fiscal Service">Crown Office and Procurator Fiscal Service</a> seized the money and prosecuted the traveller under the <a href="/wiki/Proceeds_of_Crime_Act_2002" title="Proceeds of Crime Act 2002">Proceeds of Crime Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transport">Ground transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ground transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Glasgow_airport_bus_2019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/First_Glasgow_airport_bus_2019.jpg/220px-First_Glasgow_airport_bus_2019.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/First_Glasgow_airport_bus_2019.jpg/330px-First_Glasgow_airport_bus_2019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/First_Glasgow_airport_bus_2019.jpg/440px-First_Glasgow_airport_bus_2019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5360" data-file-height="3573" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Glasgow_airport_bus_2019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Airport express buses are painted in a distinctive livery.</div></div></div>\n<p>The airport is currently linked to Glasgow City Centre by Glasgow Shuttle bus service 500. This is run by <a href="/wiki/First_Glasgow" title="First Glasgow">First Glasgow</a> under contract to Glasgow Airport. Started in 2011, the service runs 24 hours a day, direct via the M8 motorway. <a href="/wiki/McGill%27s_Bus_Services" title="McGill&#39;s Bus Services">McGill\'s Bus Services</a> service 757 links the airport with <a href="/wiki/Paisley_Gilmour_Street_railway_station" title="Paisley Gilmour Street railway station">Paisley Gilmour Street railway station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paisley,_Renfrewshire" title="Paisley, Renfrewshire">Paisley</a> town centre, Erskine &amp; Clydebank. This bus accepts <a href="/wiki/National_Rail" title="National Rail">National Rail</a> tickets between Glasgow Airport and any railway station.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_rail_link">Proposed rail link</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Proposed rail link">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport_Rail_Link" title="Glasgow Airport Rail Link">Glasgow Airport Rail Link</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow_Subway_and_proposed_Airport_Rail_Map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Glasgow_Subway_and_proposed_Airport_Rail_Map.svg/220px-Glasgow_Subway_and_proposed_Airport_Rail_Map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="95" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Glasgow_Subway_and_proposed_Airport_Rail_Map.svg/330px-Glasgow_Subway_and_proposed_Airport_Rail_Map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Glasgow_Subway_and_proposed_Airport_Rail_Map.svg/440px-Glasgow_Subway_and_proposed_Airport_Rail_Map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="612" data-file-height="265" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glasgow_Subway_and_proposed_Airport_Rail_Map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Proposed alignment for the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport_Rail_Link" title="Glasgow Airport Rail Link">Glasgow Airport Rail Link</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Plans for a rail link from the airport to <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_station" title="Glasgow Central station">Glasgow Central station</a> were proposed in the 2000s, shelved in 2009 and then resurrected in December 2016;<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> work is due to start in 2022, with the line expected to open in 2025.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Glasgow_Metro">Glasgow Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Glasgow Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Subway" title="Glasgow Subway">Glasgow Subway</a></div>\n<p>A planned extension of the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Subway" title="Glasgow Subway">Glasgow Subway</a> system which is proposed to include multiple light rail and elevated rapid transit lines around the city including a line to <a href="/wiki/Paisley,_Renfrewshire" title="Paisley, Renfrewshire">Paisley</a> City Centre, and two stations at Glasgow Airport. The line would be elevated at the airport and run on segregated tracks into <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> City Centre, and would most likely cancel the current plans for the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport_Rail_Link" title="Glasgow Airport Rail Link">Glasgow Airport Rail Link</a>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glasgow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span
